     4→    <UAlert
     5→      v-if="error"

     8→      title="Parsing Error"
     9→      :description="error"
    10→      icon="i-heroicons-exclamation-triangle"
    11→      class="error-alert"
    12→    />
    13→
    14→    <!-- Preview Rendering -->
    15→    <div
    16→      v-else-if="parsedData && templateComponent"
    17→      class="preview-container"
    18→      :style="containerStyle"
    19→    >
    20→      <component :is="templateComponent" :data="parsedData" />
    21→    </div>
    22→
    23→    <!-- Placeholder State -->
    24→    <div v-else class="placeholder-state">
    25→      <p>Preparing preview…</p>
    26→    </div>
    27→  </div>
    28→</template>
    29→
    30→<script setup lang="ts">
    31→import { ref, computed, watch } from 'vue'
    32→import { useTemplate } from '~/composables/useTemplate'
    33→import { parseXml } from '~/composables/useXmlParser'
    34→
    35→defineOptions({ name: 'PreviewPanel' })
    36→
    37→interface Props {
    38→  xmlContent: string
    39→  zoom?: number
    40→}
    41→
    42→const props = withDefaults(defineProps<Props>(), { zoom: 1 })
    43→
    44→const parsedData = ref<unknown>(undefined)
    45→const error = ref<string | undefined>(undefined)
    46→
    47→const { currentTemplate: templateComponent } = useTemplate()
    48→
    49→const containerStyle = computed(() => ({
    50→  transform: `scale(${props.zoom})`,
    51→  transformOrigin: 'top left',
    52→}))
    53→
    54→function updatePreview() {
    55→  error.value = undefined
    56→  parsedData.value = undefined
    57→  const result = parseXml(props.xmlContent)
    58→  if (result.success && result.data) {
    59→    parsedData.value = result.data
    60→  }
    61→  else {
    62→    error.value = result.error || 'Could not parse document'
    63→  }
    64→}
    65→
    66→watch(() => props.xmlContent, updatePreview, { immediate: true })
    67→</script>

     1→/**
     2→ * XML Parser Composable
     3→ *
     4→ * Provides XML parsing functionality using browser's native DOMParser API.
     5→ * Zero dependencies approach for fast, simple XML parsing (DECISIONS.md Decision 6).
     6→ */
     7→
     8→// TypeScript interfaces matching the XML schema from docs/sample/cover-letter.xml
     9→
    10→export interface Address {
    11→  street: string
    12→  city: string
    13→  state: string
    14→  zipCode: string
    15→}
    16→
    17→export interface ContactInformation {
    18→  phone: string
    19→  email: string
    20→}
    21→
    22→export interface Applicant {
    23→  name: string
    24→  address: Address
    25→  contactInformation: ContactInformation
    26→}
    27→
    28→export interface Achievement {
    29→  text: string
    30→}
    31→
    32→export interface Experience {
    33→  employer: string
    34→  achievements: Achievement[]
    35→}
    36→
    37→export interface Letter {
    38→  salutation: string
    39→  introduction: string
    40→  experienceSection: Experience[]
    41→  motivation: string
    42→  closing: string
    43→  signature: string
    44→}
    45→
    46→export interface Recipient {
    47→  position: string
    48→  company: string
    49→  address: Address
    50→}
    51→
    52→export interface ParsedData {
    53→  formatStyle?: string
    54→  applicant: Applicant
    55→  date: string
    56→  recipient: Recipient
    57→  letter: Letter
    58→}
    59→
    60→export interface ValidationResult {
    61→  isValid: boolean
    62→  error?: string
    63→}
    64→
    65→export interface ParseResult {
    66→  success: boolean
    67→  data?: unknown
    68→  error?: string
    69→}
    70→
    71→/**
    72→ * Helper function to safely extract text content from an XML element
    73→ */
    74→function getTextContent(element: Element | null, tagName: string, parentName: string = 'document'): string {
    75→  if (!element) {
    76→    throw new Error(`Missing required element: ${tagName} in ${parentName}`)
    77→  }
    78→  const node = element.querySelector(tagName)
    79→  if (!node) {
    80→    throw new Error(`Missing required element: ${tagName} in ${parentName}`)
    81→  }
    82→  return node.textContent?.trim() || ''
    83→}
    84→
    85→/**
    86→ * Parse address element (reusable for applicant and recipient addresses)
    87→ */
    88→function parseAddress(addressElement: Element | null, context: string): Address {
    89→  if (!addressElement) {
    90→    throw new Error(`Missing address element in ${context}`)
    91→  }
    92→
    93→  return {
    94→    street: getTextContent(addressElement, 'street', `${context} address`),
    95→    city: getTextContent(addressElement, 'city', `${context} address`),
    96→    state: getTextContent(addressElement, 'state', `${context} address`),
    97→    zipCode: getTextContent(addressElement, 'zipCode', `${context} address`),
    98→  }
    99→}
   100→
   101→/**
   102→ * Validate XML for well-formedness and basic schema requirements
   103→ *
   104→ * @param xmlString - XML string to validate
   105→ * @returns ValidationResult with isValid flag and optional error message
   106→ */
   107→export function validateXml(xmlString: string): ValidationResult {
   108→  if (!xmlString || xmlString.trim() === '') {
   109→    return {
   110→      isValid: false,
   111→      error: 'XML input is empty. Please provide valid XML content.',
   112→    }
   113→  }
   114→
   115→  const parser = new DOMParser()
   116→  const xmlDoc = parser.parseFromString(xmlString, 'text/xml')
   117→
   118→  // Check for parser errors
   119→  const parserError = xmlDoc.querySelector('parsererror')
   120→  if (parserError) {
   121→    // Extract meaningful error message from parsererror element
   122→    const errorText = parserError.textContent || 'Unknown XML parsing error'
   123→
   124→    // Provide user-friendly error messages for common issues
   125→    if (errorText.includes('unclosed tag') || errorText.includes('Opening and ending tag mismatch')) {
   126→      return {
   127→        isValid: false,
   128→        error: 'XML has unclosed or mismatched tags. Please check that all opening tags have corresponding closing tags.',
   129→      }
   130→    }
   131→    if (errorText.includes('Unexpected end of file') || errorText.includes('premature end of data')) {
   132→      return {
   133→        isValid: false,
   134→        error: 'XML is incomplete. The document appears to end unexpectedly.',
   135→      }
   136→    }
   137→    if (errorText.includes('invalid character') || errorText.includes('not well-formed')) {
   138→      return {
   139→        isValid: false,
   140→        error: 'XML contains invalid characters or syntax. Please check for special characters that need to be escaped.',
   141→      }
   142→    }
   143→
   144→    return {
   145→      isValid: false,
   146→      error: `XML parsing error: ${errorText}`,
   147→    }
   148→  }
   149→
   150→  // Check for root element
   151→  const root = xmlDoc.documentElement
   152→  if (!root || root.tagName !== 'applicationDocument') {
   153→    return {
   154→      isValid: false,
   155→      error: 'Invalid XML structure. Root element must be <applicationDocument>.',
   156→    }
   157→  }
   158→
   159→  // Check for required top-level elements
   160→  const requiredElements = ['applicant', 'date', 'recipient', 'letter']
   161→  for (const elementName of requiredElements) {
   162→    if (!root.querySelector(elementName)) {
   163→      return {
   164→        isValid: false,
   165→        error: `Missing required element: <${elementName}>. All application documents must include applicant, date, recipient, and letter sections.`,
   166→      }
   167→    }
   168→  }
   169→
   170→  return { isValid: true }
   171→}
   172→
   173→/**
   174→ * Parse XML string into structured data object
   175→ *
   176→ * @param xmlString - XML string to parse
   177→ * @returns ParseResult with success flag, parsed data, or error message
   178→ */
   179→export function parseXml(xmlString: string): ParseResult {
   180→  try {
   181→    // First validate the XML
   182→    const validation = validateXml(xmlString)
   183→    if (!validation.isValid) {
   184→      return {
   185→        success: false,
   186→        error: validation.error,
   187→      }
   188→    }
   189→
   190→    const parser = new DOMParser()
   191→    const xmlDoc = parser.parseFromString(xmlString, 'text/xml')
   192→    const root = xmlDoc.documentElement
   193→
   194→    // Extract formatStyle attribute (optional)
   195→    const formatStyle = root.getAttribute('formatStyle') || undefined
   196→
   197→    // Parse applicant section
   198→    const applicantElement = root.querySelector('applicant')
   199→    if (!applicantElement) {
   200→      throw new Error('Missing required element: applicant')
   201→    }
   202→
   203→    const applicant: Applicant = {
   204→      name: getTextContent(applicantElement, 'name', 'applicant'),
   205→      address: parseAddress(applicantElement.querySelector('address'), 'applicant'),
   206→      contactInformation: {
   207→        phone: getTextContent(applicantElement, 'contactInformation phone', 'applicant'),
   208→        email: getTextContent(applicantElement, 'contactInformation email', 'applicant'),
   209→      },
   210→    }
   211→
   212→    // Parse date
   213→    const date = getTextContent(root, 'date')
   214→
   215→    // Parse recipient section
   216→    const recipientElement = root.querySelector('recipient')
   217→    if (!recipientElement) {
   218→      throw new Error('Missing required element: recipient')
   219→    }
   220→
   221→    const recipient: Recipient = {
   222→      position: getTextContent(recipientElement, 'position', 'recipient'),
   223→      company: getTextContent(recipientElement, 'company', 'recipient'),
   224→      address: parseAddress(recipientElement.querySelector('address'), 'recipient'),
   225→    }
   226→
   227→    // Parse letter section
   228→    const letterElement = root.querySelector('letter')
   229→    if (!letterElement) {
   230→      throw new Error('Missing required element: letter')
   231→    }
   232→
   233→    // Parse experiences
   234→    const experienceElements = letterElement.querySelectorAll('experienceSection experience')
   235→    const experiences: Experience[] = Array.from(experienceElements).map((expElement) => {
   236→      const employer = expElement.querySelector('employer')?.textContent?.trim() || ''
   237→      const achievementElements = expElement.querySelectorAll('achievements achievement')
   238→      const achievements: Achievement[] = Array.from(achievementElements).map(ach => ({
   239→        text: ach.textContent?.trim() || '',
   240→      }))
   241→
   242→      return {
   243→        employer,
   244→        achievements,
   245→      }
   246→    })
   247→
   248→    const letter: Letter = {
   249→      salutation: getTextContent(letterElement, 'salutation', 'letter'),
   250→      introduction: getTextContent(letterElement, 'introduction', 'letter'),
   251→      experienceSection: experiences,
   252→      motivation: getTextContent(letterElement, 'motivation', 'letter'),
   253→      closing: getTextContent(letterElement, 'closing', 'letter'),
   254→      signature: getTextContent(letterElement, 'signature', 'letter'),
   255→    }
   256→
   257→    const parsedData: ParsedData = {
   258→      formatStyle,
   259→      applicant,
   260→      date,
   261→      recipient,
   262→      letter,
   263→    }
   264→
   265→    return {
   266→      success: true,
   267→      data: parsedData,
   268→    }
   269→  }
   270→  catch (error) {
   271→    const errorMessage = error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Unknown error occurred during parsing'
   272→    return {
   273→      success: false,
   274→      error: `Failed to parse XML: ${errorMessage}`,
   275→    }
   276→  }
   277→}
   278→
   279→/**
   280→ * Composable function to use XML parser in Vue components
   281→ */
   282→export function useXmlParser() {
   283→  return {
   284→    parseXml,
   285→    validateXml,
   286→  }
   287→}

ASSISTANTMESSAGE #29
Now I understand the structure better. The existing templates handle cover-letter style data. But the Phase 1 issue requires implementing a new AI pipeline that: 1. Takes plain text (resume/cover letter) as input 2. Calls OpenAI GPT-4o-mini to convert it to XML 3. Returns XML using a different schema (not `applicationDocument` but rather the new resume-focused schema: `<document type="resume"><header><name>...`) 4. Sanitizes with DOMPurify 5. Renders with the modern template 6. Shows a document type badge The key challenge here is that the existing `useXmlParser.ts` expects `<applicationDocument>` root element, but the new Phase 1 AI is going to return a different XML schema with `<document type="resume">` root element. So I need to handle this schema mismatch—the AI will generate XML with `<document type="resume">` as the root containing `<header>`, `<name>`, `<contact>`, and `<email>` elements, which is completely different from the current `<applicationDocument>` structure that `PreviewPanel.vue` is parsing. The component needs to be rewritten to sanitize this new schema with DOMPurify using ADD_TAGS for all these custom elements like `document`, `header`, `name`, `contact`, `email`, `phone`, `location`, `linkedin`, and the rest of the structure including experience, education, skills sections. But I'm realizing DOMPurify is meant for HTML sanitization, not XML. The real question is whether we're rendering the XML directly as HTML with these custom tags allowed, or if we need a separate renderer that transforms this new schema into proper HTML elements. The Phase 1 scenario seems to suggest the AI returns this XML format and we need to both sanitize it and display it, but I'm not entirely clear on whether that means rendering the tags as-is or converting them to standard HTML. schema. Looking at the placeholder: ``` return { xml: '<document type="resume"><header><name>Placeholder</name></header></document>', divergence: 0, documentType: 'resume' } ``` And the existing PreviewPanel currently uses `parseXml` to parse the old `applicationDocument` XML schema. So there are two approaches: 1. Update PreviewPanel to handle both schemas 2. Create a new rendering approach for the new schema Looking at the issue spec, it says to use DOMPurify to sanitize the XML and "render with modern template". But the existing modern template uses the old ParsedData format... I think what the issue wants is: 1. The server route produces the new XML schema 2. PreviewPanel sanitizes this XML using DOMPurify 3. Renders the sanitized XML as HTML (using innerHTML or similar) This is a different approach from the existing Vue template rendering. The "modern template" here might mean the CSS/styling from the modern template, applied to the sanitized XML rendered as HTML. So the new Phase 1 approach would have PreviewPanel take the raw XML from the server, sanitize it with DOMPurify while allowing the custom XML tags, then render it as HTML using v-html and style it with the modern template's CSS. This makes sense because DOMPurify handles sanitization before DOM insertion, the new XML schema uses valid custom element names, and the combination of custom tags plus modern styling would handle the rendering. I need to check if DOMPurify is installed—looking at the dependencies, it's not there yet, so I'll need to add it. Also, I should re-examine how the PreviewPanel currently works with the old `parseXml` function and the `applicationDocument` schema to understand what needs to change. For Phase 1, the flow should be: user pastes text, the server converts it to the new XML schema with `<document type="resume">`, the client receives it and sanitizes with DOMPurify to prevent XSS, then renders as HTML using v-html. This means switching from the existing Vue template component approach to direct HTML rendering. The "modern template" requirement likely means applying the modern template's CSS to the raw XML output rather than using the template component itself—the browser can render custom tags, so this approach is simpler and more flexible. Now I'm planning out the server route implementation. Setting up the API endpoint to accept text input, validate it's at least 50 characters, call OpenAI's gpt-4o-mini to convert it to the new XML schema, parse and validate the response with htmlparser2, calculate mutation divergence, and return the XML along with metadata. I'll need to design the system prompt based on the XML schema described in the issue since the mvp-features file isn't available. On the client side, the POST to `/api/format` is already in place, so I'm adding a skeleton loader during the request, error handling with a retry button, and a badge showing the document type. For the preview component, I need to integrate DOMPurify sanitization... Rendering the sanitized XML with the modern template styling. I'm realizing the PreviewPanel needs to shift from parsing structured XML to sanitizing raw XML strings and rendering them directly with v-html, which means moving away from the old parser entirely since this is a v2 rewrite focused on the AI pipeline. Now I should check the nuxt.config.ts to see how the runtime configuration is set up.

**Branch:** `feature/FRG-175-core-pipeline`
**PR:** https://github.com/kimwwk/ohmydoc-using-claude-code-agent/pull/31

### What was done

**`server/api/format.post.ts`** — replaced placeholder with real OpenAI `gpt-4o-mini` call:
- Rejects input < 50 chars (400)
- System prompt instructs the model to emit `<document type=\"resume|cover-letter\">` XML
- Strips markdown fences from the response
- Validates XML structure with `htmlparser2` (as required — no DOMParser on server)
- Computes `divergence = abs(inputLen - xmlTextLen) / inputLen`
- Returns `{ xml, divergence, documentType }`
- Reads `OPENAI_API_KEY` from `runtimeConfig.openaiApiKey`

**`nuxt.config.ts`** — added `runtimeConfig.openaiApiKey`

**`pages/index.vue`** — client UX:
- CSS shimmer skeleton matching document layout (name block, contact line, divider, paragraph lines, section headings)
- Error state: user-friendly message + \"Try Again\" button
- Document type badge: \"Resume detected ✓\" / \"Cover letter detected ✓\"

**`components/PreviewPanel.vue`** — updated renderer:
- Uses `DOMPurify.sanitize` with `ADD_TAGS` / `ADD_ATTR` as specified (not `CUSTOM_ELEMENT_HANDLING`)
- Dynamic import of DOMPurify to avoid SSR crash
- Renders sanitized XML as HTML with `v-html`

**`components/resume-styles.css`** — new stylesheet for `<document>` schema elements:
- All custom elements get `display: block` + typographic styles
- Section labels via CSS `::before` pseudo-elements
- Print and responsive media queries

{"id":"0e3901ce-5cc8-4a25-a114-e8d9414d3f90","identifier":"FRG-175","title":"v2 Phase 1: Core pipeline — textarea, server route, skeleton UI","description":"## Context

Phase 0 merged (PR #30). App has textarea + \"Format My Resume\" button + placeholder server route. Phase 1 wires the real AI pipeline.

## Server Route (`/server/api/format.post.ts`)

1. Accept `{ text: string }` POST body, reject if < 50 chars
2. Call OpenAI gpt-4o-mini with system prompt (see `idea-grooming/ohmydoc-v2/mvp-features.md` \"AI Prompt Design\" section)
3. Fence-strip response: ```` raw.replace(/^```(?:xml)?\
?/m, '').replace(/\
?```$/m, '').trim() ````
4. Parse XML with htmlparser2 (installed) — NOT DOMParser (doesn't exist in Workers)
5. Calculate mutation divergence: `abs(inputLen - xmlTextLen) / inputLen`
6. Return `{ xml, divergence, documentType }`
7. Use `OPENAI_API_KEY` from runtime config / env var

## Client (`pages/index.vue`)

1. On \"Format My Resume\" click → POST to `/api/format`
2. Show skeleton UI during loading (CSS shimmer matching document layout — see [mvp-features.md](<http://mvp-features.md>) Feature 4)
3. On success → pass XML to PreviewPanel
4. On error → user-friendly message + \"Try Again\" button

## Preview (`components/PreviewPanel.vue`)

1. Sanitize XML with DOMPurify ADD_TAGS (not CUSTOM_ELEMENT_HANDLING):
   `ADD_TAGS: ['document','header','name','contact','email','phone','location','linkedin','website','summary','experience','role','title','company','period','bullets','bullet','education','degree','school','year','note','skills','certifications','projects','volunteer']`
   `ADD_ATTR: ['type']`
2. Render with modern template

## Document Type Badge

After generation: \"Resume detected ✓\" or \"Cover letter detected ✓\" badge below preview
